  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ea3b2ca0-660e-43fe-90aa-e00e0c739cac'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer6176267276419612354"><b><b>A Korean <i>Charlotte's Web<br/><br/></i>More than 2 million copies sold</b><br/>  </b><br/> This is the story of a hen named Sprout. No longer content to lay eggs on command, only to have them carted off to the market, she glimpses her future every morning through the barn doors, where the other animals roam free, and comes up with a plan to escape into the wild—and to hatch an egg of her own.<br/><br/> An anthem fo</span>
  <span id="freeText6176267276419612354" style="display:none"><b><b>A Korean <i>Charlotte's Web<br /><br /></i>More than 2 million copies sold</b><br />  </b><br /> This is the story of a hen named Sprout. No longer content to lay eggs on command, only to have them carted off to the market, she glimpses her future every morning through the barn doors, where the other animals roam free, and comes up with a plan to escape into the wild—and to hatch an egg of her own.<br /><br /> An anthem for freedom, individuality and motherhood featuring a plucky, spirited heroine who rebels against the tradition-bound world of the barnyard, <i>The Hen Who Dreamed She Could Fly </i>is a novel of universal resonance that also opens a window on Korea, where it has captivated millions of readers. And with its array of animal characters—the hen, the duck, the rooster, the dog, the weasel—it calls to mind such classics in English as <i>Animal Farm </i>and <i>Charlotte’s Web.</i><br /><br /> Featuring specially-commissioned illustrations, this first English-language edition of Sun-mi Hwang’s fable for our times beautifully captures the journey of an unforgettable character in world literature.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6176267276419612354" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I agree about reading it yourself. You don't say what age your daughter is and that is important. Its a lovely book and I would certainly recommend it<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I agree about reading it yourself. You don't say what age your daughter is and that is important. Its a lovely book and I would certainly recommend it to my daughters when they were younger - and you as her parent will be able to pick up whether its suitably challenging or not for your daughter, which I assume the ratings are about?<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_2276973657" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2276973657" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5211606-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505571524p2/5211606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2276973657?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/5211606-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5211606-julie?shelf=favorite-adoption-stories">favorite-adoption-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2276973657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer40516743856148848">Isn't it weird, how a book will sometimes speak to you from a book store or library, call your attention to it and demand that you take it home?<br/><br/>That's what happened with me and this skinny novel last week. I saw it in a book store, pictured the unread books in stacks next to my bed, and ignored it. But as I walked on by, the little hen on the cover called out my name.<br/><br/>I knew nothing about this book, other than it was translated into English from Korean lit. As I started it, I realized the pull wa</span>
  <span id="freeText40516743856148848" style="display:none">Isn't it weird, how a book will sometimes speak to you from a book store or library, call your attention to it and demand that you take it home?<br /><br />That's what happened with me and this skinny novel last week. I saw it in a book store, pictured the unread books in stacks next to my bed, and ignored it. But as I walked on by, the little hen on the cover called out my name.<br /><br />I knew nothing about this book, other than it was translated into English from Korean lit. As I started it, I realized the pull was something more; this was a story told in the spirit of <i>Watership Down</i> and <i>Animal Farm</i>; meaning, a tale of animals that live together and communicate as humans do. I don't know why, but these stories have always worked for me. I blame <i>The Bremen Town Musicians</i> in my youth.<br /><br />But, here's what's weird. This is. . . an adoption story. And I'm a mom with three kids and two adoption stories and here I am, unexpectedly meeting <i>Sprout</i>, a little hen who “had only one wish, to hatch an egg and watch the birth of a chick.”<br /><br />Sprout, when we first meet her, appears diseased and has been left for dead in a pile of chicken carcasses. She escapes, but she's made an enemy of a relentless weasel and it seems like she'll never fulfill her dream of becoming a mother.<br /><br />She has named herself Sprout, because “a sprout is the mother of flowers, it breathes, stands firm against rain and wind, keeps sunlight, and rears blindingly white flowers. If it weren't for sprouts, there'd be no trees. A sprout is vital.”<br /><br />And, before you know it, you want Sprout to become a mother as badly as she does, and when she finds that abandoned egg in a nest, you're almost praying that it hatches.<br /><br />It does; it hatches, but it's a <i>duck</i> instead of a chick, and, while Sprout doesn't mind in the least, she is shocked to discover that she and her new baby are rejected by both the chickens <i>and</i> the ducks. The chickens think it's disgraceful; she should abandon the duck immediately to save face, and the ducks praise her for hatching the baby, but think she should relinquish the baby immediately to his “own kind.”<br /><br />And this Caucasian mother ached for Sprout and can remember so clearly boarding an airplane on a Chinese airlines and having a Chinese man spit on her, kick the back of her seat in disgust the entire flight, and then get out of his seat repeatedly to stick his finger in her face and curse in Mandarin at her. <br /><br />Then she remembers arriving back in the United States, only to have a Caucasian bus driver sneer threateningly right into her ear, “What are you lady, some kind of <i>Christian</i>? You think you can do this good deed with your Chinese baby and be martyred forever in Heaven?”<br /><br />Oh, yes. I've been Sprout. I've been badgered, I've been stared at (as have my kids), and I've had some of the nastiest things said to me that aren't worth strengthening by repeating. <br /><br />Like Sprout, I have walked through the barnyard and heard, “A chicken hatching a duck! What a ridiculous sight!”<br /><br />I have had to spread my wings wide over their heads to protect them and bolster them inside for the day they become too big for my wingspan.<br /><br />Like the baby duck, who becomes <i>Greentop</i>, my daughters may one day wonder, “What if the ducks never accept me?”<br /><br />And, like the hen Sprout, I may need to advise them, “Do what you want to do. Ask yourself what that is.”<br /><br />This is a book that is written in simple language, with a simple message: life is tough, the enemy is ever-present, but you have courage and joy inside you. Seek what you want and need and stand tall.<br /><br />The final paragraph is almost paralyzing in its strength and beauty.</span>
  <a data-text-id="40516743856148848" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12773985135290108023"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447661748i/17034633._SX540_.jpg' width='200' height='150' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/>Image source: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://farm4.staticflickr.com/3917/15263126215_e552bc9ffa_b.jpg'>https://farm4.staticflickr.com/3917/1...</a><br/><br/>A strange little book I picked up by mistake. A pleasant enough mistake, though.<br/><br/>It’s a Korean fable about dreams, identity/difference, courage, and what makes a mother. It may not be startlingly original or uniquely profound, but that’s part of its charm.<br/><br/>It could easily be a children’s book, though the beautiful, simple illustrations are perhaps too few for younger children.<br/><br/>Sprout is an aging hen in a coop, who longs to hatch an egg.<br/><br/>She esca</span>
  <span id="freeText12773985135290108023" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447661748i/17034633._SX540_.jpg" width="200" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Image source: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://farm4.staticflickr.com/3917/15263126215_e552bc9ffa_b.jpg">https://farm4.staticflickr.com/3917/1...</a><br><br>A strange little book I picked up by mistake. A pleasant enough mistake, though.<br><br>It’s a Korean fable about dreams, identity/difference, courage, and what makes a mother. It may not be startlingly original or uniquely profound, but that’s part of its charm.<br><br>It could easily be a children’s book, though the beautiful, simple illustrations are perhaps too few for younger children.<br><br>Sprout is an aging hen in a coop, who longs to hatch an egg.<br><br>She escapes the coop, escapes a weasel, and finds a newly-hatched, abandoned egg. But it’s a duck egg. <br><br>She loves her baby as her own, but the fowl in the farmyard are outraged. The poor ducking (Greentop is not an ugly ducking) is ostracised by hens and ducks, being neither one thing nor the other. To a Brit, this shouts a message about multiculturalism, mixed-race children, and inter-racial adoption, but to Koreans, it may relate more to North and South Korea.<br><br>Nature or nurture? Both, of course, but rather than a compromise between the two, here, nature’s genes for swimming and flying are irrepressible, but it’s the nurture of mothering that defines a mother. (I tried to ignore reductionist lines like "If I can't lay an egg, what's the point of my life?")<br><br>I was struck that in English, "mothering" is something anyone can do, whereas "fathering" is limited to those who sire a child. That hides an important truth.<br><br>Adult or child, male or female, we all need both sides of the mothering/mothered relationship in our lives. <br>With that, maybe we can learn to fly.<br><br><b>Quotes</b><br><br>•	“Ever since she named herself, she’d gotten into the habit of noticing events occurring outside the coop.” Names are empowering.<br><br>•	“Yes, you’re both hens, but you’re different.”<br><br>•	“Just because you’re the same kind doesn’t mean you’re all one happy family.”<br><br>•	“I’m sitting on it, and I’m going to raise it. Surely that makes it my baby.”<br></span>

<div id="review_1445940868" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1445940868" />
    <a title="Richard Derus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus"><img alt="Richard Derus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494992210p2/3920693.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1445940868?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard Derus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard Derus" href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus">Richard Derus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1445940868" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17285465993066821040">Rating: 3* of five<br/><br/><b>The Publisher Says</b>: This is the story of a hen named Sprout. No longer content to lay eggs on command, only to have them carted off to the market, she glimpses her future every morning through the barn doors, where the other animals roam free, and comes up with a plan to escape into the wild—and to hatch an egg of her own.<br/><br/>An anthem for freedom, individuality and motherhood featuring a plucky, spirited heroine who rebels against the tradition-bound world of the barnyard, <i>The Hen</i></span>
  <span id="freeText17285465993066821040" style="display:none">Rating: 3* of five<br /><br /><b>The Publisher Says</b>: This is the story of a hen named Sprout. No longer content to lay eggs on command, only to have them carted off to the market, she glimpses her future every morning through the barn doors, where the other animals roam free, and comes up with a plan to escape into the wild—and to hatch an egg of her own.<br /><br />An anthem for freedom, individuality and motherhood featuring a plucky, spirited heroine who rebels against the tradition-bound world of the barnyard, <i>The Hen Who Dreamed She Could Fly</i> is a novel of universal resonance that also opens a window on Korea, where it has captivated millions of readers. And with its array of animal characters—the hen, the duck, the rooster, the dog, the weasel—it calls to mind such classics in English as <i>Animal Farm</i> and <i>Charlotte’s Web</i>.<br /><br />Featuring specially-commissioned illustrations, this first English-language edition of Sun-mi Hwang’s fable for our times beautifully captures the journey of an unforgettable character in world literature.<br /><br /><b>My Review</b>: <i>Jonathan Livingston Seagull</i> meets <i>Babe</i>. To compare the book to <i>Charlotte's Web</i> is damned near heresy. In every generation, there's another fable of Independence Declared by ____ and the Struggles of _____ to <i>xxxx</i>. This is the 21st century's international publishing phenomenon in the genre, which the provincial, smugly self-satisfied Murrikin Megapublishers got 15 years after most places did.<br /><br />If you're 14 and a sad, lonely, misunderstood girl, this is ideal to stuff into your locker. Also a grandmother's ideal gift for same. Older folks who've just become grandparents, adoptees and their mommies, those who are sentimental as all get-out, queue up for your copy.<br /><br />The illustrations are so very spare and lovely and evocative that I gave the silly text 3 stars. But my <u>serious</u> objection to the book is that the hen's one true dream, the longing of her soul, the reason she's ready to fight a <b>weasel</b> fagodsake is:<br /><blockquote>She want to become a real hen and hatch an egg.</blockquote><br />So, in other words, Motherhood Makes the Hen.<br /><br />This is not a message I think needs further spreading. It has metastasized in our various cultures to the point that rich first-world folks go buy themselves a baby girl at the Chinese Baby Bazaar, or spend absurd amounts of money doing medical hoo-hah and get themselves their very own genetic descendants.<br /><br />With seven billion people on the planet, this obsession, this personal value marker, needs to be re-thought and revised.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17285465993066821040" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1435221213" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1435221213" />
    <a title="Zanna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22591633-zanna"><img alt="Zanna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512813535p2/22591633.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1435221213?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zanna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zanna" href="/user/show/22591633-zanna">Zanna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">veg*ns, feminists</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22591633-zanna?shelf=y-a">y-a</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22591633-zanna?shelf=translated">translated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22591633-zanna?shelf=into-the-forest">into-the-forest</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1435221213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer460520796151092393">The Hen Who Dreamed She Could Fly is about freedom and the interconnectedness of life, demonstrating that rather than a freedom of ONE liberation involves autonomous participation in a community of living beings<br/><br/>The protagonist, a caged laying hen, has already committed her first act of rebellion at the opening of the story: she has carefully and lovingly observed an acacia tree through an unintentional gap in her enclosure and concluded that the SPROUT is the key to the cycle of life that the tr</span>
  <span id="freeText460520796151092393" style="display:none">The Hen Who Dreamed She Could Fly is about freedom and the interconnectedness of life, demonstrating that rather than a freedom of ONE liberation involves autonomous participation in a community of living beings<br /><br />The protagonist, a caged laying hen, has already committed her first act of rebellion at the opening of the story: she has carefully and lovingly observed an acacia tree through an unintentional gap in her enclosure and concluded that the SPROUT is the key to the cycle of life that the tree's seasonal variations embody. She <b>names herself</b> after the part of the tree that 'gives birth' to the leaves and flowers, claiming her right to self-determination and a place in the cycle of being.<br /><br />As an exploited prisoner Sprout is forced to produce food for humans. The farmer and 'the farmer's wife' see animal bodies as property: machines that make profit or food for them. Sprout's eggs are taken away as she cherishes the hope of hatching a chick and becoming a mother. Although her eggs are not removed from the cycle of social reproduction totally (they are eaten) she herself has no further part in their existence after her body has produced them. In protest she refuses to continue laying. Sprout's rejection of her exploitation links, I think, to the <a>reproductive justice</a> framework developed by African American women, which centres the body autonomy and health issues of marginalised women, including those who are incarcerated. An RJ framing would affirm Sprout's right to become a mother as well as her refusal to perform reproductive labour.<br /><br />Sprout's marginalised status is further explored when she finds herself among the group of animals in the yard who have a slightly greater measure of freedom but are still exploited by the farmers. The group rejects her and she is told to return to the coop. Only very reluctantly do they allow her shelter and they drive her away from their food violently although there seems to be plenty of it. A wild mallard duck who has managed to gain a precarious place at the margin of the elitist community, which is also deeply divided along species lines, is Sprout's only friend. She enjoys foraging free range in the fields, but does not feel safe as she has met a dangerous predator, the weasel.<br /><br />Disrupting the haughty speciesism of the yard animals, Hwang makes Sprout a surrogate mother to an orphaned duckling. Thus, parenting is not biologically determined or bounded and inter-species relationships are affirmed. Sprout's mallard friend tells her 'we look different […] but we cherish each other in our own way'. Later she repeats this idea to her adopted son.<br /><br />Life in the wild is fraught with anxiety and struggle, but in a confrontation with the weasel, Sprout realises that her liberated existence with her son has been happy. The circle of beings is doubly affirmed by her interactions with her nemesis.<br /><br />This edition is a very attractive little book with extremely cute drawings by Nomoco. It's suitable for young readers and anyone who enjoyed <i>The Little Prince</i>, but from a vegan feminist perspective it's also a near perfect fable = )</span>
  <a data-text-id="460520796151092393" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen"><img alt="Helene Jeppesen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528006866p2/21992464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1299526025?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helene Jeppesen" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen">Helene Jeppesen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1299526025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8807697577933767494">This was a really cute story told from a hen's perspective. It's a story that deals with animals, but it's really about aspects of life that are really important and relevant; such as motherhood, bullying and protectiveness. <br/>This book definitely provided me with a different reading experience since I was inside a hen's head. It was refreshing to read from this point of view, and I especially liked how I could still very much identify with this hen. Even though the story is about important topics</span>
  <span id="freeText8807697577933767494" style="display:none">This was a really cute story told from a hen's perspective. It's a story that deals with animals, but it's really about aspects of life that are really important and relevant; such as motherhood, bullying and protectiveness. <br />This book definitely provided me with a different reading experience since I was inside a hen's head. It was refreshing to read from this point of view, and I especially liked how I could still very much identify with this hen. Even though the story is about important topics, I didn't feel an urge to continue reading, though. It was an endearing and entertaining story, but in my eyes it wasn't a masterpiece. Still, I'm very happy I read it and it has probably changed my view on hens and how they live their lives. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2091412559" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17297182964179183458">This is a much beloved story from South Korea about an egg-laying hen named Sprout. Sprout dreams of nothing more than to roam free and be able to hatch an egg and care for a chick of her own. This allegory is often compared to Charlotte's Web. With a cast of memorable talking animals and themes including friendship, longing, unconditional love, and self-sacrifice, this delightful tale is worth the hour or two invested.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1002482600" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1002482600" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1605591-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1252166169p2/1605591.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1002482600?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/1605591-christine">Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1605591-christine?shelf=literature-south-korean">literature-south-korean</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1605591-christine?shelf=minority-and-women-writers">minority-and-women-writers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1605591-christine?shelf=animal-fiction">animal-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1002482600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13336587939614690943"><br/>	One wonders if Aesop knew how much of good thing he had when he wrote his fables, that years and years later, that the idea of animal characters being used as allegory would still be current. Today, most people think of Animal Farm when discussing allegories using animals, but perhaps in later years it will be Animal Farm and the hen Sprout, the heroine of this charming and deeply moving tale.<br/><br/>	While no doubt highly influenced by Korean culture, Sien-Ma Hwang’s story also draws on Western classi</span>
  <span id="freeText13336587939614690943" style="display:none"><br />	One wonders if Aesop knew how much of good thing he had when he wrote his fables, that years and years later, that the idea of animal characters being used as allegory would still be current. Today, most people think of Animal Farm when discussing allegories using animals, but perhaps in later years it will be Animal Farm and the hen Sprout, the heroine of this charming and deeply moving tale.<br /><br />	While no doubt highly influenced by Korean culture, Sien-Ma Hwang’s story also draws on Western classics like “The Ugly Duckling” and “The Little Red Hen”. Sprout starts her story trapped in a cage fulfilling her heart breaking duty of laying eggs. She eventually gets out and struggles to find a place in the outside world, a place where she has longed to be but that comes with dangers that she didn’t know about it. Due to a series of circumstances, she finds herself in charge of an egg.<br /><br />	While the book is mediation about family, love, and motherhood, it is also a close look at nature as well as the influence of man on nature. The fictional character closest to Sprout in the history of literature seems to be HCA’s Little Mermaid. The idea of scarf ice for the greater purpose and the morality of it is something that both characters share to a great degree.<br /><br />	It also is impossible to read the beginning of the book and to not think of North Korea. Sprout’s journey starts in the most horrific way (and it will most likely insure that you confine chicken eating to free range). But if the coop is North Korea than is the barnyard the South? It is better but not a paradise. The allegory works because becoming who you are transcends society, even a benign one.<br /><br />	It’s strange considering how short the book is the large impact that it has. Putting the book down, leaving Sprout in some ways is like cutting off a limb, disconnecting your mind from something, it’s a wrenching feeling. This is despite the almost starkness of the prose. If the Narnia books are an allegory overboard, Sprout’s story is an allegory grown properly.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13336587939614690943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2139403551" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2139403551" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4643325-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535048395p2/4643325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2139403551?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/4643325-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4643325-paul?shelf=women-of-colour-2017">women-of-colour-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2139403551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7987326666375303114">4.5 stars<br/>Not the sort of thing I usually read, this is a parable/fable which can easily be read by adults or children with line drawings between each chapter. It is the story of a battery hen who has named herself Sprout who dreams of being free and being able to actually hatch an egg of her own. She looks out of her cage enviously at the animals who are free in the farmyard. Events combine so that Sprout does escape. She is not accepted in the hierarchical world of the farmyard because of where</span>
  <span id="freeText7987326666375303114" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br />Not the sort of thing I usually read, this is a parable/fable which can easily be read by adults or children with line drawings between each chapter. It is the story of a battery hen who has named herself Sprout who dreams of being free and being able to actually hatch an egg of her own. She looks out of her cage enviously at the animals who are free in the farmyard. Events combine so that Sprout does escape. She is not accepted in the hierarchical world of the farmyard because of where she has come from, although one of the male, ducks, called Straggler, does speak not her. He is also an outsider. Not being in the farmyard leaves her in danger from the main predator in the area, a weasel. <br />Straggler and another duck produce an egg away from the farmyard, but Straggler’s mate is taken by the weasel. Sprout sits on the egg until it hatches, during which time Straggler is also taken by the weasel. Sprout is left to bring up a duckling alone with opposition from the animals in the farmyard and the ducks on the reservoir and Sprout’s struggles with the weasel, the weather and with bringing up a duckling make up the rest of the book.<br />Of course this works on a number of levels and a great deal could be read into it. One of my GR friends Richard has referred to it as Jonathon Livingston Seagull meets Babe (wish I’d thought of that!). The whole covers racism, liberation, bullying, friendship, marginality (almost reminding me of Wacquant here), parenting (not biologically determined) and struggle. I did have some concern that the message was that Sprout could only be fulfilled through motherhood, but I think there is much more to the tale than this. Sprout isn’t a biological mother; she rears a duckling not a chick and the messages are obvious and very apt for a divided and hierarchical society like the one I live in. It works as a simple fable as well and Sun-Mi Hwang has written something that will capture imaginations of adults and children alike.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7987326666375303114" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/712322671" />
    <a title="Diane S ☔" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s"><img alt="Diane S ☔" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598402138p2/4159922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/712322671?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane S ☔" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane S ☔" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s">Diane S ☔</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer712322671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16602578269170865615">3.5 South Korean novelette that can be read as a morality tale, a fable, or a metaphor. I just know that I absolutely adore Sprout, she is one plucky chicken that goes against the established routines at the farm to fulfill her desires. Of course she has quite a bit of luck and quite a few trials. It is a wonderful story about a mother's unconditional love. Setting what you love free and doing what you think is in the child's best interest, above your own wants and desires. <br/><br/>Wonderful little stor</span>
  <span id="freeText16602578269170865615" style="display:none">3.5 South Korean novelette that can be read as a morality tale, a fable, or a metaphor. I just know that I absolutely adore Sprout, she is one plucky chicken that goes against the established routines at the farm to fulfill her desires. Of course she has quite a bit of luck and quite a few trials. It is a wonderful story about a mother's unconditional love. Setting what you love free and doing what you think is in the child's best interest, above your own wants and desires. <br /><br />Wonderful little story with plenty of meaning and a wonderful cover. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16602578269170865615" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_890004908" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/890004908" />
    <a title="adrianna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9724006-adrianna"><img alt="adrianna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390098981p2/9724006.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/890004908?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="adrianna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="adrianna" href="/user/show/9724006-adrianna">adrianna</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer890004908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3153732189668988327">I didn't expect much from that book when I first picked it up, but it turned out to be such an important read. It is about one brave hen, a very brave one, who decides to make a big change in her life in order to fulfill her dream. It is safe to say that Sprout (that's the hen's name) is a true heroine.<br/>This book is about motherhood, friendship, and love. It is about disappointments. And it is about being different. But above all, it is about courage and dedication.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3549766045" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3549766045" />
    <a title="Mridula Gupta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67269664-mridula-gupta"><img alt="Mridula Gupta" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598259878p2/67269664.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3549766045?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mridula Gupta" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mridula Gupta" href="/user/show/67269664-mridula-gupta">Mridula Gupta</a>

        rated it

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67269664-mridula-gupta?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3549766045" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2656125834737934238">The life of a parent (or someone who wants to be a parent) summed up in 90 odd pages (illustration and all). This short story is an allegory, for misfits who are bullied by the society for having different ideologies and appearances. Sprout, initially kept in a coop, rebels to find her way into the barn and then fosters a duck egg. Her journey from a hen with big dreams to an outcast and then a mother is incredibly powerful and inspiring.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2757440439" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2757440439" />
    <a title="Vishy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5555413-vishy"><img alt="Vishy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307126420p2/5555413.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2757440439?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vishy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vishy" href="/user/show/5555413-vishy">Vishy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781780745343" href="/book/show/20754546-the-hen-who-dreamed-she-could-fly">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2757440439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13852406353652933314">'The Hen Who Dreamed She Could Fly' by Sun-Mi Hwang was highly recommended to me by two of my friends. I borrowed it from one of them and read it in one breath today. <br/><br/>Sprout is a hen who lives in a farm. She is reared for the eggs she lays. Her dream is to get out of the enclosure she is in, go and walk around the yard outside, lay eggs and watch chicks hatch out of them, and bring up her little ones. But the humans who keep her, take away her eggs, as soon as she lays them. One day she stops la</span>
  <span id="freeText13852406353652933314" style="display:none">'The Hen Who Dreamed She Could Fly' by Sun-Mi Hwang was highly recommended to me by two of my friends. I borrowed it from one of them and read it in one breath today. <br /><br />Sprout is a hen who lives in a farm. She is reared for the eggs she lays. Her dream is to get out of the enclosure she is in, go and walk around the yard outside, lay eggs and watch chicks hatch out of them, and bring up her little ones. But the humans who keep her, take away her eggs, as soon as she lays them. One day she stops laying eggs. The humans feel that her time is up and throw her and other hens, who have stopped laying eggs, into a pit. There a weasel is eyeing her as a potential next meal. But a mallard duck called Straggler helps her out and takes her to his barn and provides her temporary accommodation. But the other birds and animals in the barn compel her to leave the next day. Sprout leaves the security of the barn, goes outside finds her own food and lives a freespirited life - a life which is unusual for hens. One day she discovers an egg. It appears to be freshly laid. Deep feelings gush our of her and she decides to sit on the egg to make it hatch. At some point her friend Straggler finds her there and he helps her with food. When the incubation period is over, the egg hatches. A small bird comes out of it. Sprout thinks that it is a strange-looking chicken. She loves her baby very much. What happens after that is amazing. <br /><br />I can continue telling the story till the end, but I will stop here. I will let you read it for yourself and experience the pleasure and the joy it has to offer. <br /><br />I loved 'The Hen Who Dreamed She Could Fly'. It is a beautiful book about a mother and her baby, about the joys and challenges of parenting, about how the only way to parent our kids is to unconditionally love them, nurture them, help them see their true selves and realize their potential, not hold them back but help them to fly high, and if they come back enjoy their homecoming, and if they don't, be satisfied that one has done a good job. Parenting is the most difficult job in the world, and the most selfless, but also the most beautiful and the most rewarding. Sprout shows how she is an awesome mom and though her baby is very different from her, she helps him see his true self and realize his potential. There is atleast one surprise in store for the reader towards the end, and when I reached the last page, I cried, because all beautiful things have to come to an end. But as Ellie Harp says in 'One Tree Hill' - "Every song has a coda, a final movement. Whether it fades out or crashes away, every song ends. Is that any reason not to enjoy the music?" I enjoyed this particular music composed so beautifully by Sun-Mi Hwang, singing the glories of the beautiful life of the awesome mom Sprout and her beloved baby. <br /><br />'The Hen Who Dreamed She Could Fly' is a beautiful book which will uplift your spirits when you are down, and if you are feeling uplifted already, it will make your spirits soar high. Go read it ☺️</span>
  <a data-text-id="13852406353652933314" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9450512647225937782">I was a very lucky goodreads first reads winner of this sweet book. "The Hen Who Dreamed She Could Fly" by Sun-Mi Hwang. This book is from Korea and has sold over two million copies. It is getting ready to come to other countries. I can see why this sold so many copies. it is a very sweet story about a hen named Sprout. she lived on a farm and was used to lay eggs.   <span id="freeText9450512647225937782" style="display:none">I was a very lucky goodreads first reads winner of this sweet book. "The Hen Who Dreamed She Could Fly" by Sun-Mi Hwang. This book is from Korea and has sold over two million copies. It is getting ready to come to other countries. I can see why this sold so many copies. it is a very sweet story about a hen named Sprout. she lived on a farm and was used to lay eggs. After laying her last egg forthe farmers she was doomed to be sent off to her death. she survives and manages to escape. her only wish is to lay an egg that would hatch a baby chick for herself. she just wants to be a mommy. her wish comes true "sort of" when she finds an egg away from the farm. she sits on it to keep it warm and soon becomes a mommy to a duckling she names baby.I won't give away too much more of the plot. there are hens, ducks, dogs, and weasels to add to the story. think part "Babe" and a Animal Farm. where the animals speak to each other. This is a gem of a book. If you like books with animals, birds etc. you will love this wonderful story.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1460714014?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it

<div id="review_3448131988" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3448131988" />
    <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos"><img alt="Sotiris Karaiskos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407195235p2/18940246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3448131988?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sotiris Karaiskos" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos">Sotiris Karaiskos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789603646914" href="/book/show/21942987">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3448131988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8897794965054510954">A fairy tale that is not only addressed to children, I dare say that for the most part the things that the author is talking about could hardly be understood by younger readers. You see, without being an allegory, this story contains many messages on many important issues. The hen of our story was born to have a specific role on the farm, to have a specific position in the hierarchy imposed by strict rules. Things get complicated when she decides to do something different, to choose a different </span>
  <span id="freeText8897794965054510954" style="display:none">A fairy tale that is not only addressed to children, I dare say that for the most part the things that the author is talking about could hardly be understood by younger readers. You see, without being an allegory, this story contains many messages on many important issues. The hen of our story was born to have a specific role on the farm, to have a specific position in the hierarchy imposed by strict rules. Things get complicated when she decides to do something different, to choose a different way of life that is not in line with her social status and type, and in the end to experience motherhood on her own terms. Of course for the farm society, all this is unacceptable and as expected it comes into conflict with our heroine and leads her into exile, so as not to offend them with her behaviour and set a bad example to children. This, however, does not discourage her at all as her desire to follow her heart is so great that the consequences do not frighten her at all. So we follow her course, we are moved by her courage and determination, we are outraged by the narrow-mindedness of her opponents and in the end, we are left with the feeling and hope that love can break all ties.<br /><br /> In other words, in this tale, some situations are not far from reality. We live in a society that, as much as it wants to be called liberal, as much as it claims that it is not bothered by diversity, as much as it wants to give us the illusion that it does not prevent mobility has a strict hierarchy and strict rules for what is allowed and what is not. Of course, questioning is allowed, but those who dare to do it, those who choose to follow their heart and their own sense of right and wrong will be on the sidelines like the hen of our story. For them, however, there is no other way, whatever the consequences, no matter how much pain they suffer and that is in my opinion what remains after reading this very beautiful story.<br /><br />Ένα παραμύθι που δεν απευθύνεται μόνο στα παιδιά, τολμώ να πω μάλιστα ότι σε μεγάλο μέρος του τα πράγματα για τα οποία μιλάει η συγγραφέας δύσκολα θα μπορούσαν να γίνουν αντιληπτά τους μικρότερους αναγνώστες. Βλέπετε, χωρίς να πρόκειται ακριβώς για κάποια αλληγορία, αυτή η ιστορία περιέχει πολλά μηνύματα για πολλά σημαντικά ζητήματα. Η κότα της ιστορίας μας γεννήθηκε για να έχει έναν συγκεκριμένο ρόλο στο αγρόκτημα, για να έχει μία συγκεκριμένη θέση στην ιεραρχία που επιβάλλουν οι αυστηροί κανόνες. Τα πράγματα γίνονται περίπλοκα όταν αποφασίζει να κάνει κάτι διαφορετικό, να επιλέξει έναν διαφορετικό τρόπο ζωής που δεν συνάδει με την κοινωνική της θέση και το είδος της και στο τέλος να βιώσει τη μητρότητα με τους δικούς της όρους. Φυσικά για την κοινωνία του αγροκτήματος όλα αυτά είναι απαράδεκτα και αναμενόμενα έρχεται σε σύγκρουση με την ηρωίδα μας και την οδηγεί στην εξορία, για να μη τους σκανδαλίζει με τη συμπεριφορά της και να δίνει το κακό παράδειγμα στα παιδιά. Αυτό, όμως, δεν την πτοεί καθόλου καθώς η θέλησή της να ακολουθήσει την καρδιά της είναι τόσο μεγάλη που οι συνέπειες δεν την φοβίζουν καθόλου. Έτσι παρακολουθούμε αυτή την πορεία της, συγκινούμαστε με το θάρρος και την αποφασιστικότητα της, εξοργιζόμαστε με την στενοκεφαλιά των αντιπάλων της και στο τέλος μένουμε με την αίσθηση και την ελπίδα ότι η αγάπη μπορεί να σπάσει όλα τα δεσμά.<br /><br /> Με άλλα λόγια μέσα σε αυτό το παραμύθι υπάρχουν καταστάσεις που δεν απέχουν πολύ από την πραγματικότητα. Ζούμε σε μία κοινωνία που όσο και αν θέλει να λέγεται φιλελεύθερη, όσο και αν ισχυρίζεται ότι δεν ενοχλείται από τη διαφορετικότητα, όσο και αν θέλει να μας δίνει την ψευδαίσθηση ότι δεν αποτρέπει την κινητικότητα, στην πραγματικότητα έχει μία αυστηρή ιεραρχία και αυστηρούς κανόνες για το τι επιτρέπεται και τι όχι. Φυσικά η αμφισβήτηση επιτρέπεται αλλά αυτοί που θα τολμήσουν να την κάνουν, αυτοί που θα επιλέξουν ακολουθήσουν την καρδιά τους και τη δική τους αίσθηση για το σωστό και το λάθος θα βρεθούν στο περιθώριο όπως η κότα της ιστορίας μας. Για αυτούς, όμως, δεν υπάρχει άλλος δρόμος, όποιες και να είναι οι συνέπειες, όσο πόνο και να υποστούν και αυτό είναι κατά τη γνώμη μου αυτό που μένει μετά την ανάγνωση αυτής της πολύ όμορφης ιστορίας.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8897794965054510954" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_753448669" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/753448669" />
    <a title="Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9104633-jason"><img alt="Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518977342p2/9104633.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/753448669?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/9104633-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9104633-jason?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9104633-jason?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer753448669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1780140237132903892">NETGALLEY <br/><br/><br/>Laced with a heavy emphasis on themes such as family, transition, adulthood, and death, this novel traces the life of a hen, her offspring, and the various life transitions speckled in between. This simple tale recalls previous works, including charlotte's Web, Love You Forever, as well as echos of primary themes often seen and explored in Haruki Murakami's work. <br/><br/>The downside of this novel is that it is overly literal in the way it explores these themes. Compared to the works listed ab</span>
  <span id="freeText1780140237132903892" style="display:none">NETGALLEY <br /><br /><br />Laced with a heavy emphasis on themes such as family, transition, adulthood, and death, this novel traces the life of a hen, her offspring, and the various life transitions speckled in between. This simple tale recalls previous works, including charlotte's Web, Love You Forever, as well as echos of primary themes often seen and explored in Haruki Murakami's work. <br /><br />The downside of this novel is that it is overly literal in the way it explores these themes. Compared to the works listed above, it separates itself from the pack by being too simplistic; an approach that will ultimately lead to its failure. Rather than taking on a more abstract tone, Hwang decides to write in a simple style that is heavily on metaphors. Unfortunately this does not work. She would have been fairly successful if she used one of these techniques—a heavy emphasis on metaphors or a simple style of exploring life transitions—, rather than both, and if she painted these themes with a light wrist, rather than heavy, forced brushstroke. What I mean by the latter is that it's essential to embrace a light hand when explore life transitions using metaphors, and it is more successful if these references are covert, written in a more abstract form, such as Murakami's work. Sometimes quiet is delicious.<br /><br />Yes, the beauty of the prose alone is something that may intrigue readers. Taken at face value, the simplistic style is approachable, if one does not pay attention to the overt and weighty emphasis on life and lessons. If you were to simply look at this as a hen who finds her dreams coming true, then it may be a winner. However, like I previously mentioned, this does not work, given the heavy analytical prose. <br /><br />One may question the translation, however, and even go to such lengths as to explore how the translation to English may have deadened the meaning, damaged the tone, and wrecked the prose. Perhaps in its original language this book flourished. This is something to keep in mind while reading The Hen Who Dreamed She Could Fly. However, one also must return to this version, and in this particular English version this novel just fell flat. <br /><br />2.5</span>
  <a data-text-id="1780140237132903892" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

      <a href="/user/show/22522336-muhammad-ahmed-siddiqui">Muhammad Ahmed Siddiqui</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1790277745" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4657624296000911126">Sprout, the hen that wishes to raise its own egg for a change, is a champion for freedom, dreams and hopes. She chooses the name "Sprout" for herself because it represents growth, change and the tiny spark that grows a huge tree. She is incessantly hopeful about raising her own chick someday. She dreams of going outside the coop and the cage and live freely under the acacia tree. <br/><br/>Through Sprout the author explores the everyday struggles that many of us face. Be it loneliness, alienation among ou</span>
  <span id="freeText4657624296000911126" style="display:none">Sprout, the hen that wishes to raise its own egg for a change, is a champion for freedom, dreams and hopes. She chooses the name "Sprout" for herself because it represents growth, change and the tiny spark that grows a huge tree. She is incessantly hopeful about raising her own chick someday. She dreams of going outside the coop and the cage and live freely under the acacia tree. <br /><br />Through Sprout the author explores the everyday struggles that many of us face. Be it loneliness, alienation among our own kind and struggling to deal with monotony that demands delivery and excellence every minute of the day. Importance of Sprout's existence is tightly wound to her egg laying capacity. She conforms to this role till she starts questioning and dares to dream. With that dream begins her journey of rebellion, friendships, heartache, joy, dream, motherhood and ability love the egg she protected. She welcomes the baby duck that hatches out of the egg she was sitting on and accepts it as is. The acceptance is easy and she slips into the role of motherhood as easily. <br /><br />Heavy with metaphor, this little book leads to a conclusion after Sprout struggles existing in the wild and fighting her nemesis. Sun-mi Hwang explores oppression, marginalizing for profit, bias, bias based on social standing, adoption, friendship, dreams and hopes. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4657624296000911126" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3282926393313289949">This was a charming little fable about a hen called Sprout, who just wants to escape her cage and hatch an egg of her own.<br/><br/>It follows themes of identity, motherhood, love, freedom, names, life, death, and nature. It could also be read as a reflection of human society and our systems of oppression. That makes it all sound quite serious and dull, but it's not. It's just charming. The characters are wonderful little creations and I thoroughly enjoyed reading it.<br/><br/>It's one to be read in one sitting if </span>
  <span id="freeText3282926393313289949" style="display:none">This was a charming little fable about a hen called Sprout, who just wants to escape her cage and hatch an egg of her own.<br /><br />It follows themes of identity, motherhood, love, freedom, names, life, death, and nature. It could also be read as a reflection of human society and our systems of oppression. That makes it all sound quite serious and dull, but it's not. It's just charming. The characters are wonderful little creations and I thoroughly enjoyed reading it.<br /><br />It's one to be read in one sitting if at all possible, and I'm sure that the majority of people would enjoy it.</span>

    <a title="Lata" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13126933-lata"><img alt="Lata" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525485137p2/13126933.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2018828551?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lata" href="/user/show/13126933-lata">Lata</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101615966" href="/book/show/31425569-the-hen-who-dreamed-she-could-fly">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13126933-lata?shelf=auth-f">auth-f</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13126933-lata?shelf=2020-read">2020-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13126933-lata?shelf=2020-tbr-cleanup">2020-tbr-cleanup</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13126933-lata?shelf=bipoc-author">bipoc-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2018828551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17589577956479517162">Wow, this was heartwarming and heartbreaking. So much going on in this novella-length story: motherhood, adoption, love, wrestling with the lack of acceptance by those one resembles, finding one’s strength and confidence in new experiences, and sacrificing for those we love. <br/>And the illustrations were both charming and lovely.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3247461021" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3247461021" />
    <a title="Abbie | ab_reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53055819-abbie-ab-reads"><img alt="Abbie | ab_reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545340790p2/53055819.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3247461021?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abbie | ab_reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abbie | ab_reads" href="/user/show/53055819-abbie-ab-reads">Abbie | ab_reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53055819-abbie-ab-reads?shelf=translations-read-in-2020">translations-read-in-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3247461021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2316192657744909797">The Hen Who Dreamed She Could Fly is super sweet and super sad, translated from Korean by Chi-Young Kim. We meet Sprout, a plucky egg-laying chicken at the end of her egg-laying days. Normally this would spell out the end, but Sprout defies everything (including murderous weasels and discriminatory barn animals) and continues to thrive on her own. All her life she’s dreamed of hatching her own egg, and though this seems unlikelier than ever now, she’s determined not to give up.<br/>.<br/>Though short, it’</span>
  <span id="freeText2316192657744909797" style="display:none">The Hen Who Dreamed She Could Fly is super sweet and super sad, translated from Korean by Chi-Young Kim. We meet Sprout, a plucky egg-laying chicken at the end of her egg-laying days. Normally this would spell out the end, but Sprout defies everything (including murderous weasels and discriminatory barn animals) and continues to thrive on her own. All her life she’s dreamed of hatching her own egg, and though this seems unlikelier than ever now, she’s determined not to give up.<br />.<br />Though short, it’s an absolutely beautiful book about challenging other people’s perceptions of you, accepting our differences, and having courage even in adversity. Just a lovely fable-esque tale for adults!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2316192657744909797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oYoTlaTI++d6b/BwE4EUryFjqTPt+veNcyKEKvp5WMJtqc5IUTCKpd6rhDsENB7Ztv1wsYSz64hDzfGeoSXI7Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('n2zL8jicPgbZDjCmR3eSdyzCVUAaLkBeIhMKaBILHyJTTxYvzWRPRH3KRO1QwpgBu1yMwnNnXFsS/H/cSVePDQ==')})
  }

출간되었다. 조남주 작가는 2011년, 지적 장애가 있는 한 소년의 재능이 발견되면서 벌어지는 사건을 통해 삶의 부조리를 현실적이면서도 따뜻하게 그려낸 작품 『귀를 귀울이면』으로 ‘문학동네소설상’을 받으며 데뷔했다. 시사 교양 프로그램에서 10년 동안 일한 방송 작가답게 서민들의 일상에서 발생하는 비극을 사실적이고 공감대 높은 스토리로 표현하는 데 특출 난 재능을 보이는 작가는 신작 『82년생 김지영』에서 30대를 살고 있는 한국 여성들의 보편적인 일상을 완벽하게 재현한다. 주인공 ‘김지영 씨’의 기억을 바탕으로 한 고백을 한 축으로, 고백을 뒷받침하는 각종 통계 자료와 기사들을 또 다른 축으로 삼는 이 소설은 1982년생 김지영 씨로 대변되는 ‘그녀’들의 인생 마디마디에 존재하는 성차별적 요소를 핍진하게 묘사한다. 이를 통해 작가는 제도적 성차별이 줄어든 시대의 보이지 않는 차별들이 어떻게 여성들의 삶을 제약하고 억압하는지 보여 준다. 여권이 신장된 시대, 그러나 여전히 ‘여성’이라는 조건이 굴레로 존재하는 사회에서 살아가는 한 여자의 인생을 다룬 『82년생 김지영』은 조용한 고백과 뜨거운 고발로 완성된 새로운 페미니즘 소설이자 수많은 사람들의 경험과 자료로 이루어진 ‘목소리 소설’이다. 맘충이, 여혐, 메갈리아 등 연일 새롭게 등장하는 페미니즘 화두를 관심 있게 지켜보는 독자라면 누구나 흥미롭게 읽을 수 있고 저마다 의미를 발견할 수 있을 것이다<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"3487424922588105048\" href=\"#\" <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12972387227599305149">Hwang Sun-mi (born 1963) is a South Korean author and professor who is best known for her fable The Hen Who Dreamed She Could Fly, which has also been made into a successful animated film in South Korea, Leafie, A Hen into the Wild.<br/>She was Born in 1963, Hwang was unable to attend middle school due to poverty, but thanks to a teacher who gave her a key to a classroom, she could go to the school and</span>
  <span id="freeText12972387227599305149" style="display:none">Hwang Sun-mi (born 1963) is a South Korean author and professor who is best known for her fable The Hen Who Dreamed She Could Fly, which has also been made into a successful animated film in South Korea, Leafie, A Hen into the Wild.<br />She was Born in 1963, Hwang was unable to attend middle school due to poverty, but thanks to a teacher who gave her a key to a classroom, she could go to the school and read books whenever she wanted. She enrolled in high school by taking a certificate examination and she graduated from the creative writing departments at Seoul Institute of the Arts and Gwangju University, and from graduate school at Chung-Ang University. She lives in Seoul, South Korea.Hwang is an adjunct professor at the Faculty of Literature in the Seoul Institute of the Arts. Hwang's career as a writer began in 1995, and since then she has published nearly 30 books over various genres. She is most famous for her work "The Hen Who Dreamed She Could Fly" which was also made into a movie that broke Korean box office records for animated films, earning nearly 7 billion won in its first month of release.<br /><br />Awards:<br />Nong-min Literay Award (1995)<br />Tamla Literary Award (1997)<br />SBS Media Literary Award (2001)<br />Sejong Children's Literature Prize (2003)[7]<br />The Best Book of the Year in Poland (2012)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12972387227599305149" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
